  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_0091d193-30fa-45b4-af97-1c7ab073d792'
      });

Essun, a woman living an ordinary life in a small town, comes home to find that her husband has brutally murdered their son and kidnapped their daughter. Meanwhile, mighty Sanze -- the world-spanning empire whose innovations have been civilizat</span>
  <span id="freeText18173733172710521189" style="display:none"><i>original cover of ISBN <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=0316229296" title="0316229296" rel="nofollow noopener">0316229296</a>/<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=9780316229296" title="9780316229296" rel="nofollow noopener">9780316229296</a></i><br /><br />This is the way the world ends. Again.<br /><br />Three terrible things happen in a single day. Essun, a woman living an ordinary life in a small town, comes home to find that her husband has brutally murdered their son and kidnapped their daughter. Meanwhile, mighty Sanze -- the world-spanning empire whose innovations have been civilization's bedrock for a thousand years -- collapses as most of its citizens are murdered to serve a madman's vengeance. And worst of all, across the heart of the vast continent known as the Stillness, a great red rift has been torn into the heart of the earth, spewing ash enough to darken the sky for years. Or centuries.<br /><br />Now Essun must pursue the wreckage of her family through a deadly, dying land. Without sunlight, clean water, or arable land, and with limited stockpiles of supplies, there will be war all across the Stillness: a battle royale of nations not for power or territory, but simply for the basic resources necessary to get through the long dark night. Essun does not care if the world falls apart around her. She'll break it herself, if she must, to save her daughter.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18173733172710521189" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<div id="review_882976712" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/882976712" />
    <a title="Cezara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10812008-cezara"><img alt="Cezara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523449042p2/10812008.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/882976712?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cezara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cezara" href="/user/show/10812008-cezara">Cezara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer882976712" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12344846713467043565">Yes, 5 full stars for this one because it's everything I want in a fantasy book. I will explain.<br/><br/>I don't read fantasy and sci-fi because I like magic or space ships or laser swords or what have you. I read fantasy and sci-fi because I want to see something new, and there's no other genre that allows this much freedom of imagination, this much flexibility and bending of reality and this much room for "what ifs". The genres are ripe with tropes and cliches even so, and I'm at that point where it pa</span>
  <span id="freeText12344846713467043565" style="display:none">Yes, 5 full stars for this one because it's everything I want in a fantasy book. I will explain.<br /><br />I don't read fantasy and sci-fi because I like magic or space ships or laser swords or what have you. I read fantasy and sci-fi because I want to see something new, and there's no other genre that allows this much freedom of imagination, this much flexibility and bending of reality and this much room for "what ifs". The genres are ripe with tropes and cliches even so, and I'm at that point where it pains me to have to read again through a story about the noble hearted what's-his-face who saves the land of medieval-Europe-plus-elves-and-dragons with the help of the wise mentor and the pretty princess. Show me something else, something truly weird, I say! And N. K. Jemisin delivered. <br /><br />Let there be a world wracked by earthquakes and volcano eruptions, she says, restless and hostile. Let there be apocalypse-level events every hundred years or so. Let this world be inhabited by people who believe the Earth hates them, who value survival above all else, and have organized their society around making sure some of them will make it through the years of darkness, and famine, and poisonous air and water that follow such geologic disasters. Let there be among them those who have the power to control the earthquakes, to start and stop them at will, and let that society hate them, while doing their best to exploit them at the same time. Let there be another sentient species, strange creatures of stone whose motivations are unknown, who share this world with humans. <br /><br />Then come the the details. The mysterious ruins of the many civilizations that came before this one, some considerably more advanced. Their artifacts endure to this day, their purpose unknown and maybe unknowable now that their makers have been dead for thousands of years. The harshness and ruthlessness of a society living on the brink of extinction, where value is based on usefulness and where, come Seasonal Law, those deemed useless are left to die in the wastelands. The purely utilitarian approach to building in a world where a balcony is unquestionable proof of foolishness or privilege, where decorations are a waste of time and resources since they'll be wiped out in a few years without fail. The surprisingly advanced science, focused - unsurprisingly - on geology, chemistry and physics. The hatred and exploitation of the orogenes, those who have power over the earth itself, by a society that both fears them and desperately needs them if it is to survive. The secrets and the lies and the rewriting of history and the suppression of lore by those who want to keep the orogenes willing slaves. The horrifying abuse, and the inescapable brainwashing, but the training and education too. A system meant to make them more powerful and more powerless at the same time so that it may better make use of them. <br /><br />And then Jemisin pushes further. She goes so far out of the medieval Europe setting that she ends up on the Equator. She makes the other sentient race truly alien, as a different sentience should be, lest you end up with just stranger looking humans. She makes the humans different races, and *gasp* doesn't put the paler one in charge. Just as the characters span the gradients and combinations of human races, they span human sexuality too, from straight to gay with blurry boundaries all over the place. There's love and family and sex, but they're not the kind of relationships you're used to. Why should they be? This is not our world with some magic, mythical creatures, and sword fighting mixed in. This is something else. Something new. <br /><br />And yet, as you read, you get the feeling that this <i>could</i> be our world with some magic and some mythical creatures mixed in. You get the feeling that it <i>was</i> this sort of world at some point, and then something maybe went wrong, and everything had to change, to adapt, and this is the inevitable result. The world is strange, but it's not strangeness for strangeness's sake. It all makes sense, everything fits together, and while you can see that some things could be different, you understand perfectly well why they're not. It's like a gnarled and twisted tree growing on a rocky windswept mountain top. It's not like other trees, but not because someone decided to take an ax to it and make it as different looking as possible. No, once the seed was planted, there simply was no other way it could grow.<br /><br />I can't say more, especially about the characters and the story line, without spoilers, even though I feel I could rant about this book for days on end. Go read it. I can't begin to imagine the level of skill required to create a world so different, and then make it feel so real. N.K. Jemisin deserves your attention. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12344846713467043565" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1452492180" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1452492180" />
    <a title="Rick Riordan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25375513-rick-riordan"><img alt="Rick Riordan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442449448p2/25375513.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1452492180?book_show_action=true">Nov 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rick Riordan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rick Riordan" href="/user/show/25375513-rick-riordan">Rick Riordan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1452492180" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2183745330357550614">I picked this one up because I greatly enjoyed Jemisin's Hundred Thousand Kingdoms, but this novel was even better. Jemisin blew me away with her world-building and beautiful writing. It's the tale of an alternate earth called the Stillness, which is plagued by constant seismic activity. This leads to frequent near-extinction events called "Fifth Seasons" that keep humans on their toes. The evidence of past civilizations litters the planet -- ruined cities, incomplete 'stonelore' handed down fro</span>
  <span id="freeText2183745330357550614" style="display:none">I picked this one up because I greatly enjoyed Jemisin's Hundred Thousand Kingdoms, but this novel was even better. Jemisin blew me away with her world-building and beautiful writing. It's the tale of an alternate earth called the Stillness, which is plagued by constant seismic activity. This leads to frequent near-extinction events called "Fifth Seasons" that keep humans on their toes. The evidence of past civilizations litters the planet -- ruined cities, incomplete 'stonelore' handed down from earlier generations, and strange obelisks that float through the atmosphere like low-altitude satellites and serve no apparent purpose. The civilization that we meet in this book, the Sanze Empire, has survived for centuries by harnessing the power of orogenes -- people born with an innate ability to control their environment. The orogenes can stop earthquakes or start them. They can save cities, or draw power from living creatures and "ice" them. Their powers are terrifying yet essential, so the empire develops a caste of Guardians who have the power to neutralize the orogenes when necessary. The orogenes are held in contempt and called "roggas" by ordinary humans. Despite all their power, they cannot control their own lives. They are either hunted down and destroyed or sent to the Fulcrum to be trained and used by the empire. Imagine Hogwarts, if Hogwarts treated its students like chattel. The world Jemisin creates is as horrific as it is brilliant.<br /><br />My advice is to give the book at least fifty pages before passing judgment, because it takes a while to understand what is going on. There is a lot of terminology to get used to, and the book is told in three intertwining narratives that at first don't seem to match up, but once you get into the world and into the story, it is a fantastically rewarding read. I can't say much about the plot without giving away some of the wonderful surprises, but if you want to read about a truly dystopian world that holds a mirror to the darkest of human motivations, this novel will haunt you long after you finish it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2183745330357550614" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1567118098" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1567118098" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1567118098?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1567118098" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1980229227710753043">This book is beautiful, this book is smart, this book is oh so heartbreaking, and this book is a masterpiece. This is one of those books that make you feel absolutely guilty for giving out five stars to other books. This book is unlike anything I've ever read, but it felt so seamlessly woven. This book mirrors the society we live in today and makes you think about all those uncomfortable topics you'd rather ignore and pretend do not exist. This book has the best representation I've ever read in </span>
  <span id="freeText1980229227710753043" style="display:none">This book is beautiful, this book is smart, this book is oh so heartbreaking, and this book is a masterpiece. This is one of those books that make you feel absolutely guilty for giving out five stars to other books. This book is unlike anything I've ever read, but it felt so seamlessly woven. This book mirrors the society we live in today and makes you think about all those uncomfortable topics you'd rather ignore and pretend do not exist. This book has the best representation I've ever read in a SFF novel. This book is deserving of all the hype, all the praise, and every ounce of love it's received. This book easily is now one of my favorite books of all time.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Let's start with the end of the world, why don’t we?”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />This story is set in a world called the Stillness, where earthquakes, volcanic eruptions, and other terrible things impacting the earth are constantly happening, but there are people who are able to manipulate the earth to ease them. These people are called orogenes and even though they are continually saving the world they are constantly oppressed slaves. This world has convinced everyone that orogenes are dangerous and need to be controlled at all costs. It is illegal to harbor orogenes and you must turn them in, even if they are your family. The price of hiding a orogene is great and most people are not willing to pay it. If a orogene isn't killed by their community before they are turned in, they are taken to a training school called the Fulcrum where they are deemed worthy enough to train <br /><br />Everyone in the Stillness is trying to survive the world's unforgiving environment. This planet is beyond unstable, because of Fifth Seasons that happens sporadically, but almost wipe out the planet each and every time. The people in this world are scared that a new Fifth Season is about to begin. And just so you understand the severe of the living conditions during a Fifth Season, here are some examples: <br /><br />➽<b>Choking Season</b> - with volcanic eruptions which caused ash that, if it didn't kill you from breathing it in, the lack of sunlight for five years would try to. <br />➽<b>Acid Season</b> - with plus-ten-level earthquakes, which caused many volcanoes that caused the water to become acidic.<br />➽<b>Boiling Season</b> - with hot spot eruptions that began underneath a great lake and made millions of gallons of steam which triggered acidic ran. <br />➽<b>Fungus Season</b> - with volcanic eruptions during monsoon season which made for perfect fungal spreading that wiped out major food supplies. <br /><br />These are just a few of the season, and without orogenes this world wouldn't be able to keep a new Fifth Season at bay. This book follows three different girls who are each struggling to survive this horrible world and struggling with their own individual journeys: <br /><br />➽<b>Essun</b> - An older woman whose husband has killed their young son, because he showed that he was a orogene. He inherited his powers from Essun, but they were keeping it hidden from their community. Essun is now off to find her husband who fled after the murder and took their daughter with him. <br /><br />➽<b>Damaya</b> - A small girl who realized she was a orogene after an accidental attack. Her family is isn't willing to pay the price of harboring her, especially since her community now knows what she is. Her parents call the authorities and she is going to be taken to the Fulcrum, where they can train and use orogenes if they are trainable and submissive. <br /><br />➽<b>Syenite</b> - A young woman who has lived the majority of her life at the Fulcrum being trained. At the Fulcrum, as you increase your learning and abilities you will earn rings that signify your power and allows you more privileges. Syenite has four rings, which is impressive in its own way, but she is now assigned to breed with the only ten ring around, so she can give the Fulcrum her child in hopes that it will be very powerful and very trainable. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Orogeny is damned useful, Syenite is beginning to understand, for far, far more than just quelling shakes.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />Yet the side characters are amazing, too. Hoa, Alabaster, Tonkee, Innon, all of them, along side these three women, worked their way into my heart. This whole dystopian world that only wants to kill itself worked its way into my heart. This story is and these characters are truly one of a kind.<br /><br />This book perpetuates so many healthy ideas absolutely seamlessly: <br />➽This book is unapologetically black and it's something of beauty. <br />➽This book is about systematic oppression, set in an expertly crafted SFF novel.<br />➽This book has one of the best polyamorous relationships I've ever read. <br />➽This book has bisexual and gay representation that was perfection.<br />➽This book has a wonderful transgender side character who everyone accepts without question.<br />➽This book even celebrates found families and the importance of finding your own people that will love and accept you unconditionally. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Home is what you take with you, not what you leave behind.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />This book creates so many parallels to the world we live in today. This book, hopefully, will make you think about your internalized racism and the prejudices that you hold without even realizing it. The reason so many of us think the way we do today, in 2017, is because our world has told us to think this way without even being given a chance to think differently. This book even has a fictionalized slur for orogenes that made my stomach turn every time I read it. This book is raw and painful at times, so very painful, but it's such an important story. And I'm still unsure if I've ever read anything as sad as the node maintainers in all of my life. <i>The Fifth Season</i> isn't just an amazing SFF novel, it's a parallel to our world today, and I recommend everyone not only read this novel, but to open their eyes while reading this novel. <br /><br />N.K. Jemisin did all this and wrote one of the best SFF stories I've ever read in my life. She deserves every award she won for this masterpiece, if not more. This book is deserving of all the hype, all the praise, and every ounce of love it's received. This book easily is now one of my favorite books of all time and I can't wait to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2063711531" rel="nofollow noopener">The Obelisk Gate</a>.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“This is what you must remember: the ending of one story is just the beginning of another.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />Also, please go watch the best review of <i>The Fifth Season</i> ever created, by my all time favorite Booktuber, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7391803-adriana" rel="nofollow noopener">Adriana</a>, from <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=FqxwhlcsLkU" rel="nofollow noopener"> perpetualpages</a>! Their review brings me to tears every time I watch it, and I hope my review plus theirs will make you pick up this powerful and important book with one of the best stories ever written. <br /><br /><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a> <br /><br />Buddy Read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1677866110" rel="nofollow noopener">Gelisvb</a> ❤</span>
  <a data-text-id="1980229227710753043" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1946460674" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1946460674" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1946460674?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Elle by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2018">z-read2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-characters">favorite-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-faves2018">z-faves2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=genre-experiments">genre-experiments</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=sff-high-fantasy">sff-high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=x-series">x-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=elle-recs-list">elle-recs-list</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=characters-of-color">characters-of-color</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1946460674" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9251604067348547355"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>—for all those who have to fight for the respect others are given without question.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>I'm re-reviewing this because I accidentally used up a full page of my last essay ranting about it and now I really desperately want to reread. (<i>It's September 8th, why are all of my books still in California.</i>)<br/><br/>The fact that this series won the Hugo award three years running should very quickly establish its degree of quality but I'm going to quickly point out the things that Wowed Me anyway. The writin</span>
  <span id="freeText9251604067348547355" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>—for all those who have to fight for the respect others are given without question.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />I'm re-reviewing this because I accidentally used up a full page of my last essay ranting about it and now I really desperately want to reread. (<i>It's September 8th, why are all of my books still in California.</i>)<br /><br />The fact that this series won the Hugo award three years running should very quickly establish its degree of quality but I'm going to quickly point out the things that Wowed Me anyway. The writing of this book is glorious — there’s a sardonic and a crisp tone to it, without any wasted words. The worldbuilding is wonderful and involved. (However, I admit that I tend to be really intimidated by worldbuilding-heavy books, so can I just say — this should not intimidate. Despite the level of detail and complexity, the broad plot is not too convoluted.)<br /><br />This book contains <i>several</i> plot twists that remain some of the wildest and most incredible in literature, including one that literally caused me to scream out loud. (This is partially because the last 150 pages of this book gave me so much anxiety that I think my brain short-circuited.) While there’s not necessarily always something going on, there’s always lingering tension; this world is dangerous, and we feel that, in every beat of the book. <br /><br />Oh, and the characters are just the best. There are three POVs within this book: <br />➽Essun — an older Orogene whose husband has killed their young son after he showed signs of power. Her story is told in second-person narration. She falls in with two mysterious people, Hoa and Tonkee, while looking for her daughter Nassun. <br />➽Demaya — a child Orogene taken from her parents to the Fulcrum, a training ground for Orogenes. Her plotline is horrifying. (That hand scene <i>absolutely</i> haunts me, as in it's been a year since I first read this and I still vividly remember it.)<br />➽Syenite — a young Orogene who has grown up at the Fulcrum. Syenite's storyline is my <i>favorite</i>. Also, her dynamic with Alabaster honest to god kills me. <br /><br />I was just thinking this recently after reading <i>This Savage Song</i>, but it bears repeating: a book using enemies-to-best-friends as its key dynamic is everything I have ever wanted and I am blessed. Alabaster and Syenite, y’all. Holy fuck. I want to read 300000000 pages of them being deep-level best friends with a romantically-overtoned but still deeply platonic bond. I would die for them. (As I've now finished this series, I'm going to say it: I <i>really</i> wish they interacted more in the following books.)<br /><br />Putting aside the fact that this book consumed my waking hours and the fact that Syenite could kill me and I would thank her. The thing that resonates with me about this book and this series in general is that its central question is this: in a world that barely thinks of you as human, in a world where you have to fight for the respect others receive without prompting, in a world where you are told from the beginning of your inherent inferiority, <b>how can you find a sense of being</b>? The answer, if there is one, is through love. The Fifth Season is a book of brutal acts of oppression, but love — between lead character Syenite and her friend (it’s complicated) Alabaster, or between Syenite and her daughter Nassun — is the driving force of the book, the thing that characters risk their lives for.<br /><br />As a story about how human beings can be taught to believe in themselves only as cogs in a great wheel, it is utterly gut-wrenching. <br /><br />And in a book driven by an all-black cast, and several queer leads — the most prominent three side characters are a gay man, a bi man, and a sapphic trans woman — this feels especially significant. The fantasy setting trope of a minority culture heavily coded as being some other race is nothing new; what is new, however, is the fact that Orogenes are, in most cases, the point-of-view characters, and the lens through which we see this new world. <br /><br /><a href="https://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52545435" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/jespergayhey" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://www.youtube.com/channel/UCVIY_GxZIuclzsIw9CLSe3g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9251604067348547355" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1783986134" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1783986134" />
    <a title="Petrik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik"><img alt="Petrik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568016775p2/59458347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1783986134?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petrik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petrik" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Mix of high fantasy &amp; Sci fi fans</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1783986134" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5100209737258773528"><b>4.5/5 Stars<br/><br/>I will not start my review for this book with some praises. Don’t get me wrong, this is an amazing book <i>(oh shit I just did)</i>, but I’d like to start this review instead by saying patience is virtue is apt here.</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“For all those that have to fight for the respect that everyone else is given without question.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/><br/><i>This book and my review will be dedicated to all of you.</i><br/><br/>The Fifth Season, the first book in the Broken Earth trilogy is, in my opinion, a book that will truly require some </span>
  <span id="freeText5100209737258773528" style="display:none"><b>4.5/5 Stars<br><br>I will not start my review for this book with some praises. Don’t get me wrong, this is an amazing book <i>(oh shit I just did)</i>, but I’d like to start this review instead by saying patience is virtue is apt here.</b><br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“For all those that have to fight for the respect that everyone else is given without question.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br><i>This book and my review will be dedicated to all of you.</i><br><br>The Fifth Season, the first book in the Broken Earth trilogy is, in my opinion, a book that will truly require some patience for you to read. It took me around 80 pages to get used to everything in the book and truly start getting invested in it. That’s quite a lot of pages needed, sure there’s a great reason for this but in my opinion sacrificing the first 20%, even if the culmination of it was great. I’m not surprised if a lot of people DNF this book just from the 20%, I almost DNF it myself, it’s also the only reason why this book didn’t receive a full 5 stars rating from me. But trust me; you won’t regret reading this through to the end.<br><br>Think of a jigsaw puzzle. You start with the big picture, the box or cover of the puzzle. In the case of this book, you started with the passage “This is the way the world ends for the last time”, but you have no idea how it happens and what’s going on, what’s the catalyst? To process this, it’s really easy, read the book. You’ll probably think at this point “you don’t say?” but once you started, you’ll probably think of DNFing quickly. Like assembling a jigsaw puzzle, it’s easy to do it, you just need the patience to fit all the pieces. Brandon Sanderson praised Jemisin highly in her writing and storytelling and you know what? He’s right. Jemisin stated that The Broken Earth trilogy is the most challenging books she ever wrote, just from the first book I can already see why. I can’t imagine how much research and planning were done for the creation of this book. I think of the plot of this book as an intricate story that gets better and easier to read the more you progressed, just like how assembling jigsaw puzzle started overwhelming but gets easier and more addictive the more you progressed.<br><br>Jemisin has also done a stellar job in her characterization. Essun, Damaya, and Syenite have become one of the best written female characters I’ve ever read. Their journey, struggle, background, personality, determination are all written in a way that will make you truly care about them. <br><br><b>Picture: Essun by Miranda Meeks <i>(The cover of Fifth Season limited edition by Subterranean Press)</i></b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1502306354i/23548791._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Not only that, the side characters here are also unique and equally engaging. For those of you who are begging for diversity in their read, rest assured that you’ll find them here. You want LGBT? Oh, you’ll get it, a lot, with a passage like a “cock rubbing on oily cock”, I don’t think you can ask for more in that aspect. People of color? Brown, black, white, it’s there and they’re all well written.<br><br>Taking place in a world called The Stillness; Jemisin’s world-building is wonderful, vivid, and atmospheric. Accompanied with a rich history and an intricate magic system called Orogene, which deals with the manipulation of thermal, kinetic energy to address seismic events, almost everything about this book is Earth shatteringly good. One thing to note though, most of the terminologies here isn’t explicitly explained. You have to understand what the names are through the context provided by the narration. If you’re impatient in trying to understand the terminologies, you can just go straight to the back of the book to read the detailed explanation, there’s a whole detailed section there. <br><br>Before I close my review, I must tell you about the prose here. The way this book is written is a complete culture shock to me, especially Essun’s POV. It’s the first time I read a combination of 2nd POV narrative, done in present tense, and combined with an omniscient element so it took me a while to get into it. Damaya and Syenite’s POV are easier to read as they were done in 3rd person and present tense. It felt odd at first, but after the first 20%, it became so addictive to read. Jemisin’s prose is beautiful and enchanting, and definitely suitable for the story she’s telling here.<br><br>By the end of this book, I arrived at the conclusion that The Fifth Season is one heck of a start to a trilogy. It’s superb, highly original, and also a fantastic mix of high fantasy and sci-fi that can only be achieved by top-tiered authors. This book has won tons of awards, look them up if you want, there are too many to list here. However, let me tell you that those awards are truly well deserved.<br><br><i>You can find <a href="http://booknest.eu/reviews/26-pat-reviews/719-thefifthseason" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a> and the rest of my Adult Epic/High Fantasy &amp; Sci-Fi reviews at <a href="http://booknest.eu/review/patrick" rel="nofollow noopener">BookNest</a></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="5100209737258773528" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1378950304" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1378950304" />
    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508811508p2/4213258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1378950304?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=transhumanism">transhumanism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=dystopia-yes-pls">dystopia-yes-pls</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=2016-shelf">2016-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=worldbuilding-sf">worldbuilding-sf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=fanboy-goes-squee">fanboy-goes-squee</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=reality-bending">reality-bending</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=top-one-hundred">top-one-hundred</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1378950304" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6031811164862488054">Edit, 10:52 pm, tonight. :) N.K. Jemisin is the WINNER!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!! :) :) :) :) Was there any doubt?<br/><br/><br/>Old Review (from a few hours ago):<br/><br/>Re-Read 8/20/16, the day the Hugo Awards Ceremony is to take place for the novel I voted for. :) Coincidentally, I'll be reading the sequel tomorrow. :)<br/><br/>So was it as good as I remember? Actually, better. But that's mostly because I'm in on the trick and the secret of the MC is is laid bare and the whole novel then becomes a character exploration for me as we</span>
  <span id="freeText6031811164862488054" style="display:none">Edit, 10:52 pm, tonight. :) N.K. Jemisin is the WINNER!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!! :) :) :) :) Was there any doubt?<br /><br /><br />Old Review (from a few hours ago):<br /><br />Re-Read 8/20/16, the day the Hugo Awards Ceremony is to take place for the novel I voted for. :) Coincidentally, I'll be reading the sequel tomorrow. :)<br /><br />So was it as good as I remember? Actually, better. But that's mostly because I'm in on the trick and the secret of the MC is is laid bare and the whole novel then becomes a character exploration for me as well as a jaw-dropping mountain-load of quakeworthy World Building and awesome implications.<br /><br />Since I first read this, I read her trilogy and loved it, but what can I say? I still loved this one even more. It speaks to me right down to the absolutely horrible revelations, the personal impacts, the hopes, the fears, the successes... oh, especially the successes... and of course, the question of WHAT THE HELL IS GOING ON. :)<br /><br />To say this book is full of questions is to say that a Jane Austen book is full of lace. It's kind of obvious. The question is: What the hell is the lace up to?<br /><br />Jemisin is fantastic for mythology and mythology building, but what is best about this book is the sense of long history and cycles and the deep feeling like it is all headed somewhere huge. And it is. Just let me ask you... What DID happen to the moon? ;)<br /><br />If you haven't read this yet, then you're a fool. :) It's deeply textured in all ways, and its not just the fact that the gods are chained or that we killed Father Earth's only child. It's pretty obvious that this is a deep time future Earth, too, and everything seems to seriously point toward a mind-blowing explanation beyond recurring extinction events. :) Which happen anyway, so yeah, let's get down to the real reasons, shall we? <br /><br />WHY. :) Oh so yummy. :)<br /><br />Looking forward to the awards ceremony tonight. Let's see if my top choice made it! :)<br /><br /><br />Original Review:<br /><br />This is my first N. K. Jemisin, and I'm truly ashamed that I hadn't gotten around to her writing before now. I'm just putting that out right away, because this shame is all my own, and it is deep.<br /><br />Secondly, this feels like an intensely personal novel, to me, and for me, although maybe nobody will ever know why, except me. The way she treats the volcanoes and the earthquakes make me seethe with jealousy and rage, because it is just so damn good.<br /><br />And thirdly, I'm stuck straddling the line between how much I enjoyed the POV developments and how they eventually revealed something truly great by the end and how much I wish I had known the secret from the very start. It wouldn't have taken much. Just another line following each heading. There would have been no confusion, no mystery. But no, it is as it is, and I'm very likely going to have to reread the novel to pick up any possible failings of my inconsiderate attention span before I dive into the second novel that follows this.<br /><br />So what am I trying to say, here? That I'm a miserable failure who is taking this novel way too seriously and admits that he may have missed too much on the first read because the novel was too dense for his little brain? Possibly.<br /><br />But what I'm really saying is that this novel has skyrocketed to one of the topmost favorite novels that I've ever read, that I'm squeeing about it, and that I think I've just found my newest favorite author of all time.<br /><br />I like to think that I'm fairly well read. I like to think I have a fairly discriminate palate that shows in my reviews, even if they don't always show in something as simple as a star on a bar. I like to think that I can pick out works of deeply fine quality and works that have obviously been borne quite bloodily from an author's head, like Athena, only with much more gore. This is one of those damn fine novels that just REEKS of imagination, forethought, CRAFT, and one hell of a fine setup, a fine conclusion, and finally, a fantastic and sharp new setup.<br /><br />I remember the moon. I thought of it throughout this novel. Its having been missing throughout all these damn cataclysms caused me as much grief as the idea that the Fifth Seasons are actually huge diebacks on the Earth, recurring endlessly ever since we killed the moon in some mysterious and immense SF past. We have people with amazing powers, almost godlike in scope, having undergone so much social and historical upheavals, themselves, that no one even knows their history any longer, or why they chose to chain themselves.<br /><br />We have our main character and her shadow, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[seen semi-confusedly through different names and time periods, from childhood to adulthood to middle age; the last being the present, shown to us through the POV of her shadow in second-person. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> developing to a final convergence that is a truly wonderful reveal, while leaving us with even greater questions and a truly immense possible conflict. As if supervolcanoes and earthquakes and their control or release weren't enough conflict, right? We've the makings of one of the biggest revenge stories I've ever had the pleasure to read.<br /><br />It's almost as if I'm reading a quality SF novel that has been allowed the freedom to go Super Sayan on me. <br /><br />And so my jaw drops. <br /><br />Am I utterly amazed after reading this? Yes. Hell yes.<br />Do I have any reservations with the author's writing, timing, storytelling, subject, characters, or reveals? No. Hell no.<br /><br />I do want so say one thing after reading the afterward, though. Thank you, Ms. Jemisin for not giving up on this amazing novel. All of your blood, sweat, and tears have brought forth something truly great. I am indebted to you, personally, for changing my life and my expectations about what can actually be pulled forth from a great novel. You did something Big. Thank you!<br /><br /><br />Update 4/27/16<br /><br />And so now we learn that this novel has been nominated for both the 2016 Hugo and the Nebula!<br />By my review above, I'm pretty certain I've expressed how much I love this book, and that has not changed one bit. If I was in a position to scream from my soapbox to say to the Nebulas that this is the clear winner, I would. As it *is*, I CAN scream from my soapbox to the Hugos and say it. :)<br /><br />I mentioned in my review for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24876258.The_Aeronaut_s_Windlass__The_Cinder_Spires___1_" title="The Aeronaut's Windlass (The Cinder Spires, #1) by Jim Butcher" rel="nofollow noopener">The Aeronaut's Windlass</a>, another book that also got the Hugo nomination for this year, that there really should be two separate categories for Standalone Novels and another for Novels in a Series, because most series novels have the luxury of taking things extremely slow and build character, setting, and plot in such long sweeping epics that when we look back on them, they fairly overwhelm us if they've done their job right.<br /><br />Standalone novels can do the same thing, of course, but they have to do so economically and usually with a great deal of panache and brilliance and editing that probably makes it an entirely different kind of beast from the series novels. At this point in the SF/F genres, we have amazing examples of both and we're getting crowded in one single category that more often than not has to artificially balance series novels 3 out of 5 in 2016, crowding out a plethora of brilliant standalone novels.<br /><br />I'm fairly naturally prejudiced to separate these two forms in my head, because I'm totally invested in the characters and settings in the series, while I'm learning everything new for the first time in the standalone.<br /><br />When I think of the Hugos, I generally think of standalone novels, but I *know* it isn't true. I've recently finished reading all the Hugo winners and a very significant portion of the nominations all the way back to the start of the award. Still, I feel a bit prejudiced. I want excellent standalone novels to be recognized as such, uncontaminated by preconceptions.<br /><br />BUT. I also have to make a decision based on just how F***ing Awesome a book is, too, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19161852.The_Fifth_Season__The_Broken_Earth___1_" title="The Fifth Season (The Broken Earth, #1) by N.K. Jemisin" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fifth Season</a>, even if it is the first in a new series, is F***ing Awesome.<br /><br />I'm sure a lot of people felt the same way about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17333324.Ancillary_Justice__Imperial_Radch___1_" title="Ancillary Justice (Imperial Radch, #1) by Ann Leckie" rel="nofollow noopener">Ancillary Justice</a> when it came out, and I can't say that was the wrong choice for that year, either. :) Good is Good is Good is Good.<br /><br />So regardless of whether the category should be split up or not, out of all the choices we're presented, I think <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19161852.The_Fifth_Season__The_Broken_Earth___1_" title="The Fifth Season (The Broken Earth, #1) by N.K. Jemisin" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fifth Season</a> should shake the whole ceremony up. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="6031811164862488054" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText4580028701850238924" style="display:none">this book started off a bit rocky and slow, but i am so relieved that it eventually grew on me. i didnt love it as much as i wanted to (mainly because i misread the synopsis, so this was completely different than i thought it would be) but there is still much that i enjoyed about it. <br /><br />- this story blends both sci-fi AND fantasy. i know many books are lumped into the SFF genre, but this is the first story where both elements are present and coexist seamlessly. <br /><br />- the representation in this is endless. there is so much visibility for many different people.<br /> <br />- i like how there is a focus on the importance of family, especially the kind of family you adopt and not born into.<br /><br />i had some issues with the writing style throughout and i really wish there was more about essuns husband and daughter but, overall, this ended up proving to be a worthwhile read. i am very much looking forward to continuing the series!<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>3.5 stars</i></b></span>

<div id="review_1846252171" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1846252171" />
    <a title="Lyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn"><img alt="Lyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495541962p2/5253785.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1846252171?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyn" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn">Lyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1846252171" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6632813700304017780">Really good.<br/><br/>N. K. Jemison’s 2016 Hugo Award winner’s world building is as good as Frank Herbert or Ursula LeGuin and with magic rules as well thought out as Brandon Sanderson and with an intimate talent for complex characterization as good as Octavia Butler.<br/><br/>All comparisons aside, Jemisin’s work is wildly original and she has created a far future fantasy that provokes thought and entertains. Evoking Jack Vance’s <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/951749.The_Dying_Earth__The_Dying_Earth___1_' title='The Dying Earth (The Dying Earth, #1) by Jack Vance' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Dying Earth</a>, this is far, far in the future (if it is even Earth) where some peop</span>
  <span id="freeText6632813700304017780" style="display:none">Really good.<br><br>N. K. Jemison’s 2016 Hugo Award winner’s world building is as good as Frank Herbert or Ursula LeGuin and with magic rules as well thought out as Brandon Sanderson and with an intimate talent for complex characterization as good as Octavia Butler.<br><br>All comparisons aside, Jemisin’s work is wildly original and she has created a far future fantasy that provokes thought and entertains. Evoking Jack Vance’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/951749.The_Dying_Earth__The_Dying_Earth___1_" title="The Dying Earth (The Dying Earth, #1) by Jack Vance" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dying Earth</a>, this is far, far in the future (if it is even Earth) where some people, Orogenes, have wild earth moving kinetic powers.<br><br>And there are aliens.<br><br>In metaphor, Jemisin describes the Orogenes as both imaginatively powerful but also hated and used as slaves. In this way Jemisin uses her impressively intricate narrative to also explore themes of individuality and the One versus the Many. This allegory is especially noteworthy in our post 9/11 world where powerful individuals can affect change as much or more than a sovereign nation. <br><br>Also interesting was her use of the second person narrative structure in alternating sequences. Really don’t see that much.<br><br>Jemisin’s intricate use of tectonically powerful super humans, shunned by the rest of mankind, is also a fitting and resonant metaphor for our own responsibilities to our faltering world. The author uses the Orogenes complicated plight to reveal failings in our responsibility to our Mother Earth (interestingly changed to Father Earth in her story). <br><br>Recommended.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1557146837i/27465281._SY540_.jpg" width="320" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="6632813700304017780" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Bloody stinking fish, this was <b>painful as shrimp</b>. <br/><br/><b>99,99999%</b> of you <b>People of Despicable Book Taste</b> (PoDBT™) thought this was deliriously mind-blowing and scrumptiously original and fantabuliciously well written and all that crap, which can mean only one thing: <s>
  <b>
    <u>you</u>
  </b>
</s> I read the book <b>terribly wrong</b>. Strange. That has rarel</span>
  <span id="freeText13099353574719963058" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1423050384ra/13581493.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br>💀 <b>DNF at 38%</b>. <i>Please someone give me a medal.</i><br><br><i>The gif is strong is this one. Consider your little barnacled selves warned.</i><br><br><b>This was such a delightful read</b>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1490601881i/22325754.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Just kidding</b>. Bloody stinking fish, this was <b>painful as shrimp</b>. <br><br><b>99,99999%</b> of you <b>People of Despicable Book Taste</b> (PoDBT™) thought this was deliriously mind-blowing and scrumptiously original and fantabuliciously well written and all that crap, which can mean only one thing: <s>
  <b>
    <u>you</u>
  </b>
</s> I read the book <b>terribly wrong</b>. Strange. That has rarely ever happened in the past. I mean, <s>
  <b>
    <u>I</u>
  </b>
</s> you always display super human powers of <b>good judgement, enlightenment, discernment and acumen</b>, I wonder what the shrimp might have gone wrong here. I unfortunately do not have time to research this <b>most disturbing matter</b> right now (things to do, kingdoms to overthrow, puny humans to enslave and all that), so I guess I'll just have to hand the investigation over to my decapodic friends over at the <b>Murderous Malacostraca Institute of Treacherous Technology</b> (MMITT™). Moving on and stuff.<br><br><b>Soooo</b>. This lovely book right here. Where to start? The possibilities are quite endless. What is NOT to love about this <b><s>overhyped, headache inducing endeavor</s> most wondrous piece</b> of fantasy literature, really? There are just so many things! Like, I don't know, the <b>bloody shrimping writing</b>. That's definitely something <b>NOT to bloody shrimping love</b> about this book. I mean, it is written in <b>Deadly Present Tense of Spontaneous Self Combustion</b> (DPToSSC™), which tends to make me feel kinda sorta like this:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1496665469ra/22939972.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>The only exception</b> to this vicious allergic reaction is my boyfriend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/46424-sandman-slim" rel="nofollow noopener">Sandman Slim</a>. Because he's, you know, my <b>Super Hot Slightly Amoral and a Teensy Little Bit Screwed Up Homicidal Boyfriend</b> (SHSAaaTLBSUHB™) and stuff. But I ever so slightly digress. So. Somewhat <b>abhorrent</b> present tense narration? Check. This was bad enough and got my exoskeleton go all <b>blotchy and swollen and itchy and ew ew ew</b>, but it seems the author decided this wasn't an excruciatingly painful enough experience for me. So she threw in a healthy dose of <b>Bloody Shrimping Second Person Narrative from Hell</b> (BSSPNfH™), too. Bless her little soul. What a <b>heavenly enticing idea</b> that was. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1514572319ra/24793408.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Ah, yes, good old BSSPNfH™</b>! Such an enchanting writing device. Gives you the impression the author is trying to tell you <b>how to feel and what to think</b> and stuff. It really is quite <b>wonderful</b> ← <i>this might or might not be a slightly sarcastic comment. Just thought I'd point that out.</i> <b>Thank fish</b> the story isn't told in second person for its <b>entire entirety</b>, otherwise I might have DNFed it at page 4 ← <i>this thought never entered my mind, by the way. Not even for a second. Nope nope nope, absolutely not.</i> <b>So everybody and their shrimp</b> seem to think Jemisin's writing is beautiful and masterful and innovative and unique and original and <b>please somebody kill me now</b> because stuff like this: <br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>These people killed Uche. Their hate, their fear, their unprovoked violence. They.<br>(He.)<br>Killed your son.<br>(Jija killed your son.)</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1469585824ra/19833715.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Beautiful</b> and masterful and innovative and unique and original, huh? Not to be contrary or anything <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1490601881i/22325754.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <br>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, but I happen to think Jemisin's writing is <b>gimmicky</b> as fish and <b>disembodied</b> and <b>stilted</b> and <b>flat</b> and <b>unemotional</b> and <b>forced</b> and <b>impersonal</b> and <b>disconnected</b> and tries so hard to be <b>edgy and cool and clever and hip</b> that it ends up making <s>you</s> me feel like <s>you're</s> I'm reading a bloody <b>Creative Writing 101 essay</b> and damn this has to be the most <b>exasperating, tedious, lackluster, fabricated, irritating, dull thing</b> I have read in a bloody shrimping long time and it reminds me of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15839976.Red_Rising__Red_Rising_Saga___1_" title="Red Rising (Red Rising Saga, #1) by Pierce Brown" rel="nofollow noopener">Red Rising</a> which very logically makes me want to <b>shudder to death</b> and this sentence seems to be over now so you might <b>resume breathing</b> and stuff. You are <b>quite welcome</b>. <br> <br><b>I might</b> have tried to survive this taxing ordeal, had the plot been engaging enough. <b>But it wasn't, so I didn't</b>. Okay, the premise was pretty intriguing, to be disgustingly honest. The story itself, however, while not as <b>coma-inducing</b> as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11774272.The_Killing_Moon__Dreamblood___1_" title="The Killing Moon (Dreamblood, #1) by N.K. Jemisin" rel="nofollow noopener">The Killing Moon</a>, was still prime <b>Cure for Insomnia Material</b> (CfIM™). <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1518797574ra/25072112.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>But hey, it's not ALL bad</b>. The characters are as <b>flat</b> as my favorite herd of ironing boards, too! And <b>emotional</b> as a truckload of bricks! And deliciously <b>unlikable</b>! And beautifully <b>unpleasant</b>! And the scrumptiously <b>I Don't Give a Bloody Shrimping Damn Whether They Live or Die Dead Type</b> (IDGaBSDWTLoDDT™)! <b>Yay and stuff</b>! <br><br><b>The End</b>. And Stuff.<br><br>➽ And the moral of this <b>Much Underrated The Practice Known as DNFing is for Much Alleviation and Joy and Comfort and Bliss It Brings Crappy Non Review</b> (MUTPKaDNFifMAaBaCaJIBCNR™) is: most of my <s>Clueless</s> Little Barnacles <b>fangirl/fanboy/fanwhatever</b> about this book like <b>rabid thirteen year olds on crack</b>. If this were a free country, they would obviously be entitled to their <b><s>wrong</s> opinion</b>. Unfortunately for them, this is my <b>Subaquatic Empire of Doom and Destruction</b> (SEoDaD™), so they aren't. <b>Ha</b>. Oh, and by the way: <b>QED and stuff</b>.<br><br>✉ <i>A very private message to my <b>Friendly Neighborhood Trolls</b> (FNT™):</i> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1518795140ra/25071685.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479540926i/21203689._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>[<b>Pre-review nonsense</b>]<br><br><b>It's been a while</b> since I last felt so bloody shrimping <b>relieved</b> to put a book away. Oh wait, that's not entirely true. I kinda sorta felt the <b>same bloody shrimping way</b> when I DNFed the fish out of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11774272.The_Killing_Moon__Dreamblood___1_" title="The Killing Moon (Dreamblood, #1) by N.K. Jemisin" rel="nofollow noopener">The Killing Moon</a>. It's funny, the author of the book is called Jemisin, too. <b>Strange that</b>. I wonder if that's a coincidence. <b>Yeah, it probably is</b>. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1518602595ra/25057809.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Don't worry</b>, N.K. Jemisin, it's obviously not <b><s>me</s> you</b>, it's <b><s>you</s> me</b>. Then again <b>maybe not</b>.<br><br>➽ Full <b>This Overhyped Piece of Fish is One of the Most Overhyped Pieces of Fish I Have Read in a Loooong Time So Let's Get Trollin' Trolls I'm Ready for You Crappy Non Review</b> (TOPoFiOotMOPoFIHRiaLTSLGTTIRfYCNR™) to come.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

  <u>4.5 stars.</u>
</b> What you know for sure is that you're not a child. You don't want to know what would happen if you were <b>(this world is nasty)</b>. But you walk. Restlessly, you walk. At this point you're not sure it means something. You go on, though, because you're intrigued. Orogene, guardian, pirate, commless, you're part of the humanity anyway <b>(they don't think you are)</b>. You're no stranger to rules <b>(death awaits if you are)</b> yet life destroys them at times <b>(this is the way the world ends, again)</b>. </span>
  <span id="freeText3402174319176991867" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1462716908i/19034571._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>4.5 stars.</u>
</b> What you know for sure is that you're not a child. You don't want to know what would happen if you were <b>(this world is nasty)</b>. But you walk. Restlessly, you walk. Orogene, guardian, pirate, commless, you're part of the humanity anyway <b>(they don't think you are)</b>. Sometimes you wish info-dumping existed <b>(confusion is you)</b> but not anymore <b>(you just wait, it makes sense)</b>. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>(Friends do not exist. The fulcrum is not a school. Grits are not children. Orogenes are not people. Weapons have no need of friends.)</b>
</blockquote><br>They lied, didn't they? <b>(of course they did)</b> The rage <b>(or is it revenge)</b> threatens to close your throat at any moment but you are strong, so go on, go on, just a little longer. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Perhaps you think it wrong that I dwell so much on the horrors, the pain, but pain is what shapes us, after all. We are creatures born of heat and pressure and grinding, ceaseless movement. To be still is to be... not alive."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>You're not sure how it happened but you laugh. It's a strange thing, that laugh. It takes you by surprise <b>(the tears are never far)</b>. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"But this is the way the world ends. <br>This is the way the world ends.<br><i>This is the way the world ends.</i><br>For the last time."</b>
</blockquote><br>You understand, finally, and you're amazed <b>(it hurts, though)</b>.<br><br><b>Edit 31/07/17</b> : <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19161852.The_Fifth_Season__The_Broken_Earth___1_" title="The Fifth Season (The Broken Earth, #1) by N.K. Jemisin" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fifth Season</a> was even better the second time around, but I should have seen it coming : a story so intricate really screams <i>reread me, reread me</i> with pleading eyes. August 15th can't come soon enough.<br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2265597966" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2760959390421047291">Even though I struggled with it at times (we all know fantasy is not my usual genre, lol), there is no question that this book is a masterpiece. Wow. Wow wow wow. I can't wait to read everything else Jemisin has ever written. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2240416798" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2240416798" />
    <a title="Hamad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54464244-hamad"><img alt="Hamad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577880699p2/54464244.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2240416798?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hamad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hamad" href="/user/show/54464244-hamad">Hamad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=book-club">book-club</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=adult-books">adult-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=2020-reads">2020-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=paperbacks">paperbacks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2240416798" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2211683620188805828"><a href='https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/2020/01/30/the-fifth-season-review/' rel='nofollow noopener'>This Review</a> ✍️ <a href='https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Blog</a> 📖 <a href='https://twitter.com/Hamad9626' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> 🐦 <a href='https://www.instagram.com/thebookprescription/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> 📷<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Let’s start with the end of the world, why don’t we? Get it over with and move on to more interesting things.” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>★ This is my first pick for my book club “The Book Clinic” and after finishing it, I am so glad that I did choose it. I think it is a book that can be enjoyed by YA and adult fantasy readers, which was the main reason that made me pick it up.<br/><br/>★ This is my first novel I read by the author, I read her short story Emergency Skin last y</span>
  <span id="freeText2211683620188805828" style="display:none"><a href="https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/2020/01/30/the-fifth-season-review/" rel="nofollow noopener">This Review</a> ✍️ <a href="https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> 📖 <a href="https://twitter.com/Hamad9626" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> 🐦 <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebookprescription/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> 📷<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Let’s start with the end of the world, why don’t we? Get it over with and move on to more interesting things.” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />★ This is my first pick for my book club “The Book Clinic” and after finishing it, I am so glad that I did choose it. I think it is a book that can be enjoyed by YA and adult fantasy readers, which was the main reason that made me pick it up.<br /><br />★ This is my first novel I read by the author, I read her short story Emergency Skin last year and it was good but this was much better. I heard a lot of good things about this series and I guess I know why now.<br /><br />★ This is one of the books that needs patience and the more you give it, the more you will get back from it. I think it is not a light read and it needs a clear mind to enjoy it to the max. I confess that I had some things going on in my life and I was reading this as a distraction which may not have been wise on my part. The good thing is that I read it with members of my club who intensified an already awesome experience. They made me notice things that I initially missed and wow, some readers are very sharp!<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Who misses what they have never, ever even imagined?” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />★ The writing is good, the prologue was very magical and I knew from the start that I was going in for something very unique and different! The rest of the book had a more simple writing -still very good- and there are a ton of quotes that are worth stopping at and just losing your mind into. The author decided to write 3 POVs with one of them written in 2nd person, a very bold choice and a gamble that worked at the end of the day. I and almost all others who read this for the club had the same problem, the book was confusing at first with much info dump and alternating POVs which is too much at first but then gradually gets better and better and better! I don’t believe that the 2nd POV added much to the story but I ended up enjoying it and many others agree. I don’t know if it was the character that made it engaging or the storyline but it is a POV that grows on readers with every page.<br /><br />★ The characters were well written, whether they are primary characters or not. Almost every character has a role in the story and then everything makes sense at the end. The book was diverse AF and I felt that this diversity was natural and not forced to check boxes and sell copies. It was simply effortless and part of the author’s writing style! I asked my club who was your favorite POV and it was really hard to choose one. I think it is going to be a tough tie between the three! Essun’s POV -which is written as a 2nd person POV- was very good but needed time to get used to, the use of YOU and YOURS feels like shoving it up your throat as a reader and it can be annoying it first!<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“think you hate me because… I’m someone you can hate. I’m here, I’m handy. But what you really hate is the world.” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />★ The world-building may be the best thing about this book. There is too much at first but all answers are provided by the end (And new ones arise). There were 2 appendices at the end of the book that were really helpful, they help understand the terminology and seasons mentioned, I discovered them a bit late (around 30% of the story) but still found them useful specially the second one.<br /><br />★ The plot is a deep one, because this deals with important topics and I have to agree with one reader who said that if you remove the fantasy elements, it is still an important story about privileges and racism and oppression of the weak! The plot twists were hard to expect for me. But did the euphoria the book gave me at the end raise my rating? Would I still give it the same rating if I did a re-read knowing all the secrets now and I think the answer is yes because this story is simply much more than a plot twist!<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“This is what you must remember: the ending of one story is just the beginning of another.” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />★ Summary: A great book with a tough and shaky start full of info and confusion but patience is what makes it so rewarding! The characters and world-buildings were superb, the writing style and plot-twists were good too. I do recommend it for fantasy lover looking for something different, I am surely planning to continue the series soon.<br /><br />You can get more books from <a href="https://www.bookdepository.com/?a_aid=2611996" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Depository</a><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2211683620188805828" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
